[2026-03-15T02:15:07Z] Prathamesh: Audi's sweeping turn signals, also called dynamic LED indicators, have become a signature feature across all their models. Both the US and EU regulate sequential turn signals using standards that trace back to UN Regulation 48, requiring the sweep to move outward toward the signalled direction. The US went a step further in its 2021 update to SAE J588, incorporated into federal standard FMVSS 108. This forced Audi to alter their dynamic turn signal pattern for US market cars, a difference that is still visible today between US and EU versions — one of those things where once you see it, you cannot unsee it. Audi initially could not offer the signals on US cars at all, later resorting to hardware changes including separate bumper-mounted reflectors alongside software adjustments to reach compliance. What US regulatory requirement forced Audi to modify its iconic sequential turn signals? ↵ Looking for a general funda, not the exact rule.

[2026-03-15T15:25:40Z] Kartikey Pradhan: On a side note because I got reminded of it - just so if someone is looking to start a routine, or quit any habit - my experience has been transformational. I was playing league cricket every week, and it was an eye opener to what I had done to my body with alcohol, smoking, and selective/sporadic workout. It took a very hard 6-8 months to just reset the whole diet, get over the habit/addiction, build a routine of power training/swimming/cardio, making sleep and drinking water my religious practices - and once the flywheel was established, it had remarkable results on what I could do on the field, focus in long working hours, and mind-body connection. So if anyone’s looking for a peer push, this might help!

[2026-03-16T15:22:02Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: Q.	Messier’s Catalogue was too small, as astronomical discoveries accelerated in the 19th century. John Dreyer made the next attempt at compiling a list of objects in the night sky and assigning them specific identifying numbers. Dreyer’s 1888 work is known by the three-letter acronym X. X contains 7,840 objects, including galaxies, star clusters and emission nebulae. Dreyer published two supplements to X in 1895 and 1908, known as the Index Catalogues (abbreviated IC), describing a further 5,386 astronomical objects. Thousands of these objects are best known by their X or IC numbers, which remain in widespread use. Our galactic neighbor Andromeda gets the number 224 in X. ID X.

The German Minister of Education at the time declared that "a professor who preached such heresies was unworthy to teach science." At the time, German science was dominated by "Naturphilosophie," which believed that truth should come from abstract thinking and logic, not "messy" experiments and math. They called his work a "web of naked fancies." ↵ The backlash against his law was so severe that X was effectively forced to resign his teaching position at the Jesuit Gymnasium of Cologne. He spent the next six years living in poverty and obscurity, doing private tutoring in Berlin just to survive, all while the scientific community treated his greatest discovery as a joke. Id X
